his leg.  Dr. Mandel found it to be melanoma and called me after hours
to give me the news.  This was on a Friday.  On Saturday (her time off)

to her practice for tests to make sure the cancer has not traveled.  Dr. Mandel truly cares and wants to give the best possible care

better chance of getting through this because of her!!  Her staff is
great also!</review>

< Review>
I recently purchased a new car and was anxious about where I would get my windows tinted. My experience with Jet Black was pretty stellar.

1) I called the (510) phone # and spoke to an agent who got me scheduled in less than 5 minutes (also was stoked to discover this location here in San Fran.

2) Showed up and was greeted by the branch manager, Ibrahim, who showed me the different tints, a visual/physical demonstration with a heat lamp to show climate response, and a total.

3) Walked over to Gus's Community Market 3 blocks away where you can sit outside and enjoy coffee or pass by the time (which is amazing because Jet Black does not have a seating/waiting area).

4) Returned 2 hours later to an awesome job.

Cost ended up around 350 tax included-- keep in mind I chose the Ceramic tint versus the other tints (which looked also pretty stellar).

Overall, amazing job to Ibrahim and the staff. Appreciate your services both in the detail as well as making the process as a customer enjoyable.< /Review>

TL;DR: double quoted wait time, mess left inside car, trunk and no mask usage by staff / don't clean equipment before/after customers.

I came in at 2 hours and noticed they'd just began working on my car despite saying there was only 1 car ahead of me. I was scolded by the manager for coming in w/o being called - likely b/c of this discovery. He said it'd be just 30 mins. That turned out to be an hour later.

<Rate>2</Rate>< review>
We ordered two dishes: #1 KingFu Braised Beef brisket soup with tri-colored noodles and #8 "Secret eight treasure" hot sauce with knife cut noodles. The beef brisket soup was ok, a little bland and tasted like instant-noodle soup base, nothing special. The tri colored noodles felt under-cooked, hard, and clumpy. Definitely not the Taiwanese comfort food I was craving.

Then the secret eight treasure noodles... first I'll say the knife cut noodles were done pretty well... but that's about the only good thing about the dish. First it came out as a soupy noodle, I expected dry noodles mixed with the sauce based on the pictures. Putting "secret eight treasure" in a soup base is probably one of the silliest things I've seen. The whole appeal of secret eight treasure is the contrast in textures of each treasure from the crunchy peanut to the soft bean curd. Putting it all in a soup for hours on end resulted in a bland mush that had 0 contrast. And I'm pretty sure there weren't "eight" treasures in that soup... felt more like 3 or 4, and then there weren't even very much, maybe just a few spoonful and the rest was just the same bland watery soup base. Overall, very disappointed with the dish and would never order again.< /review>

<review>So I looked on Google and read the reviews so I was very skeptical a visiting. But I looked passed the reviews and come to find out this is by far the best plasma donation center I've seen in my 7 years of donating. First off all of the staff are super nice and great at their jobs. They comfort you they feed you and they hydrate you. They are very understanding when it comes to certain situations. Also the wait time is not as long as people make it seem because the experience is so great. Everything is fast and efficient and you meet some great people at this location from staff two donors. They compensate you with cash instead of a prepaid debit card. And on your first visit they tell you it's going to be 4 to 5 hours but usually it's only an hour and 30 minutes to 2 hours depending on how many people are there. The only thing is that it's so far if you are on public transportation in coming from Mid-City San Diego but it is fully worth it once you get there because the experience is amazing everybody is so nice. I even seen a you familiar faces that transferred from another location to work here so that made me feel even more comfortable. Big shout-out to this place and great job at what you do keep up the hard work. Sincerely Jonathan usher Raymond üôÇ</review>< pics>

< Review>
Although the wait is sometimes long, ESPECIALLY the first time, expect it to prevent being angry about it. It seems most of the negative reviews are from those that hate the wait or were rejected due to this place having standards which are completely reasonable. Long story short, don't expect to be in and out or assume you'll even be eligible.
The staff are mostly very friendly and I've had multiple pleasant small talks with them. (Shout out to Tony, Lily, Betty, and Minerva!)There IS one I don't like very much but shall remain unnamed :)
The establishment is very clean

The things I dislike:
-the annoying guy they play almost every time on the t.v. in the waiting area describing what they do and how you're a hero. Not that he's wrong but watch it once and you'll know what I'm talking about. Bring headphones or you're wait will feel longer.
-the temperature is kept at about 0¬∞C (freezing). I believe it's for preservation reasons but still lol. If you're sensitive to cold BRING A BLANKET.

well that's all I can think of. Despite the negatives I still give this place 5 stars due to the good it does, the friendly staff, and of course the extra money in my pocket< /Review>

<GmapID>0x80dcdf1bcfc160eb:0x3afdd224638f2d7c<//GmapID><review>To be honest, I came here because on Yelp I saw that if you came and wrote a Yelp review, you would get 50% off your next poke bowl, but sadly that deal does not exist anymore.

I got a regular bowl with three fish, but the bowl size was much smaller than other places and was kind of disappointing. When I came, there were only two workers working to serve, so the line was rather slow even though it was super short. By the time I got to pay for the order, two more workers had come, but I have to say it was disappointing to see the line move so slow. After the line cleared, the number of workers went back down to two. Can definitely see this being a problem later on.

In addition, while ordering my bowl, they ran out of ingredients and had to wait for people to make more. Definitely felt they were short-staffed. However, I was very happy I didn't have to pay more for toppings and avocado like some other poke places. Taste wise, it was fine, just like any regular poke bowl.

Parking was a struggle because it is located in The Lab: the Anti-Mall plaza.

All in all, it was an alright experience and I've definitely had better for the same price. Wouldn't go out of my way to come back again, but also wouldn't mind if I did.</review><pictures>None< /pictures></record>

< Text>
All these cookie cutter poke places are starting to feel very Chipotle if you know what I mean. If you don‚Äôt I‚Äôm saying they are vanilla, bland, unauthentic. Does that mean they aren‚Äôt good? NO. In fact they make tasty items. For rea mah broddah.

Most people who have been to Hawaii have never had poke the way Hawaiians eat poke. We grow up with this notion of Waba Grill and Flame Broiler where everything needs rice and veggies and protein. Poke when made for events a side dish, when eaten personally it‚Äôs a meal, but they don‚Äôt garnish it like all these places do. Poke is really more of a seafood salad. Poke came from workers on the dock cutting fresh fish scraps and mixing with local ingredients. They didn‚Äôt get the choice cuts, but when it‚Äôs fresh you have very little taste difference with all the sauces and seasoning they use.

What‚Äôs great about each new poke place is they doing slight variations. Like this place offers free seaweed salad (wakame) the very traditional Japanese salad we all recognize. They use biodegradable bowls, so they are trying to be environmentally forward and conscious. The rice stick, so my notion of salad is sounding a little more understandable, right? They currently offer a combo upgrade with miso and a drink with check in/review (though I think this is a limited offering).

They offering your standard fish like tuna, salmon, but what I really like is the scallop. I wish they had inamona (kukui nuts), offered oyster sauce, had limu, ogo or any other seaweed offering (not just wakame, nori, furikake). I like the avocado and garlic chip offerings, but the crab was bland and without sauce a detractor. Wish they had sambal chili offerings and were more authentic, but that‚Äôs slightly different. The salmon and yellowtail are consistent and fresh. I like that they offer ginger and that it‚Äôs so customizable. The sauces are a little tame, so err on the over side when asking for sauces. Their hot sauces also do not have much in the way of heat, if that‚Äôs your thing. I wish they had more citrus based or sauces with citrus notes. I like getting my sauces and seasonings on the salad and rice and not on the fish so much.

It‚Äôs not that busy, decent amount of seating, clean d√©cor, unmuddled with decorations. Staff is friendly and you can get as much of the sides as you want, but the fish is a little lacking in amount. I like to get my poke salads with a quail egg or oysters, but no one around here really offers both at a ‚Äúpoke‚Äù spot, just Japanese places with a poke item. Value is on par with other poke in the county, that is to say slightly overpriced. I‚Äôll come back because it‚Äôs the nearest place to my work if I need a fix, wish they kept the old menu and did poke as a split because a fish only offering would be a great snack to go along with their old menu. I really like the octopus.

The wave is upon is and ‚Äúauthenticity‚Äù is not something the masses care about, just me. Come get your Lab Poke here. I gave up on ranking poke places, they are all good, the value is always going to be a point of contention. Socal Poke is almost not even Hawaiian anymore. It‚Äôs interesting that most places at the lab are good, but not great, really lacking a few things and this is no different.</Text>

<Rating>5<//Rating>< review>
This is another build-your-own poke (BYOP) bowl place that has the formula for poke down to a science.  The portion sizes here are good and so is the fish. They also give you a few free extras that other places charge for, like seaweed salad and other toppings to go with your bowl.

In any case, here is the process: choose your base (white or brown rice, salad, or chips); then pick three or five scoops of sashimi to be piled on top (tuna, salmon, yellowtail, scallop, octopus, etc.); then sides of imitation crab and avocado; then finally various toppings including green onions, masago, wasabi, ginger, and garlic chips.

They have many different sauce options, including the standard soy sauce, spicy mayo, and others.  I was able to mix sauces here, which was excellent - other places don't always let you mix sauces for some reason.  Like my tip said, adding ponzu to the spicy original makes it pop.  It's really good.</review>

< text>
The only beef (figuratively) that I have with this place are the food portions. You can't really get full (as a marathon runner) without buying triple of everything.

However, if you're on a diet, as people in LA are wont, then you get a really delicious sampling of food. The leek soup or the clam soup are standards here. Also, the flank steak salad is made with really fresh ingredients.

Best of all is the coffee. If you need to laptop camp and can keep up with buying a coffee every two hours, this place is for you. It's not crowded during the day on week days. I'm sure they'll love your business.</text>

< Text>
They started adding a service charge here to help pay the bussers and people cooking food etc. Instead of putting the service charge on the customer maybe pay them higher wages instead? < Text>
Pretty solid coffee spot, even if I can't decide if they are a coffee shop or a restaurant!

Heard about Lamill through the coffee grapevine and came in to do a little bit of work and sample their drinks. Had the espresso and a cappuccino. The cappuccino was pretty good- good milk, didn't overpower the espresso. The espresso wasn't anything to write home about, unfortunately. Crema was a little thin and it tasted just a tad bit sour. Nothing terrible, but it didn't strike my fancy.

Service was attentive, even though I had my head in my laptop 60% of the time. Pretty cool, shabby chic decor in a quieter part of Silverlake.

Three stars for now- can't wait to come back and try their food and get the whole experience!< /Text>

Lamill Coffee is famous on Instagram and my two teenage daughters wanted to visit. I recently uploaded the review on my blog and found that their receipts has 10.5% Service charge BEFORE Sales tax(9%). Not to mention 10.5% Service charge on top of TO-GO order. I checked online and found "When this preset service charge or "mandatory tip" is added by the retailer to the customer's bill, it is subject to tax."
Is this place worth paying the mandatory tip and sales tax on top of it? Not to me.

< review>
LAMill reminds me of a fancy boutique hotel lobby, and I definitely mean that as a compliment. Great place to meet up for coffee/tea, or take your laptop and do some work on your own. It's usually pretty quiet so not the best choice for a big group dinner or anything. Another possible use for LA Mill: taking care of a Craigslist transaction like the laptop-purchase I witnessed in their sidewalk dining area, ha! A bit expensive ($6-9 for an individual pot of tea) but the specialty-ness of it all makes it worth that. Nice servers who aren't overbearing and street parking is usually available along Silver Lake Blvd.</review>
